Deteriorating Relations between Italy and Yugoslavia Cause Outrage; Vow to Resist Foreign Aggression 72

▲National News Agency, Belgrade, 21st: Relations between Yugoslavia and Italy are becoming increasingly tense, almost to the point of rupture. The matter arose from the Italian government's protest against the anti-Italian demonstrations in Cetinje and Belgrade, and the damage to two ancient stone lions on the border. Today, the Yugoslav Senate convened a meeting, and the atmosphere was extremely agitated. A resolution was passed, requesting the government to insist on protecting Yugoslavia's sovereignty and to reject any foreign aggression. The Foreign Minister did not respond to the Italian government's criticism, only saying that the letter was regrettable and without any basis, as Yugoslavia had never infringed upon Italy's interests or ideology. If Yugoslavia responded to Italy's criticism in the same manner, it would damage feelings. Now, we can only wait and see how things develop, but it must be stated that this is by no means the Yugoslav government wanting to draw swords and fight, nor is it advocating a policy of non-resistance. The Foreign Minister's speech was greeted with enthusiastic applause from the senators. It is expected that there will be continued anti-Italian demonstrations throughout Yugoslavia, especially in Dalmatia, which has been going on for a long time.

New French Prime Minister Announces Policies; Fiscal Policy Follows Precedent 73

▲Havas, Paris, 22nd: New Prime Minister Paul-Boncour read a declaration in the National Assembly today, praising former Prime Minister Herriot and his policies. Although the Herriot cabinet fell due to the vote on December 14, its policies have not been damaged. The organization of the current cabinet should be seen as an expression of willingness to inherit the policies of the previous cabinet. The current government's task is to navigate through a landscape filled with thorns. As for financial issues, the government intends to clean up finances, make up for losses, and rebuild a balanced budget. In order to achieve this goal, the government requires that all expenses be extremely tightened. All legal entities are willing to sacrifice for the country. In addition, the government also wants to find ways to reorganize public services and reduce redundant staff. Currently, it is necessary to immediately take measures to ensure that the next budget is balanced. The government is currently only requesting a one-month provisional budget (i.e., the provisional budget for January, because the current budget has not yet been passed by January). However, by January, the government may have to request a second month's provisional budget, which will include important parts of the austerity policy. Regarding the war debt issue, the government believes that in the current situation and the complex political situation in the United States, negotiations should be conducted with a very cautious attitude. The direction of these negotiations has been indicated by the vote in the Chamber of Deputies on December 14. Since December 14, Herriot and the Washington government have maintained their original relationship. The government now intends to promote negotiations to reach a comprehensive solution, so that the turmoil caused by the war debt burden on the economic recovery of various countries can come to an end. For this matter, we should cooperate with our allies, especially the United Kingdom. In addition, the government also intends to vigorously promote other international negotiations, because economic panic is not only due to economic reasons, but also due to psychological reasons. In particular, continued international unrest, mutual suspicion, and competition between nations are the main causes of economic panic.

US House Passes Beer Legalization

Dry Faction Obstructs in Every Possible Way to No Effect; Joyful Enthusiasm in the Gallery 74

▲National News Agency, Washington, 21st: After the US House of Representatives passed the beer legalization bill today by an unexpected majority, the gallery was filled with joyful enthusiasm, as if drunk, and could no longer pay attention to the Speaker and the guards' attempts to maintain order. However, when the vote was being taken, the entire chamber was silent. When the Speaker announced that the bill had passed, with 230 votes in favor and 165 against, cheers immediately erupted. Except for the 165 die-hard prohibitionists, everyone's faces were filled with joy. Before the vote, the debate was extremely fierce. The prohibition faction exhausted all means to obstruct the bill, proposing amendments almost every few minutes, but the legalization faction strongly rejected them. In the end, the prohibition faction's amendments and obstruction reached a dead end, and the entire bill was put to a vote. As a result, 93 Republicans, 136 Democrats, and members of the Farmer-Labor Party voted in favor, while only 100 Republicans and 65 Democrats voted against. Before the final vote on the bill, someone moved to reduce the legal alcohol content of beer from 3.2% to 2.75%, which also failed, showing the sentiment of the majority of the American people towards legalization. The bill will now be moved to the Senate, but its fate in the Senate is questionable, as it is said that the Senate wants to use this bill as a tool to deal with the general sales tax. The general sales tax bill is destined to meet stubborn opposition in the Senate. If this bill fails, the beer legalization bill may also be rejected.

Japan to Hold Large-Scale Air Combat Exercises Next Spring

Over 400 Aircraft to Participate, Preparing to Disrupt World Peace 75

China United Press, Tokyo, 22nd: The Japanese Army Department feels that the air force is a powerful weapon for the future. In the incidents in Shanghai and the three northeastern provinces, if the Japanese army did not have air support, the casualties of the Japanese army would have been several times higher. In order to intensify research on large-scale air combat, the Japanese Army Department has decided to hold large-scale air combat exercises in Aichi and Gifu prefectures in March next spring. Seven air regiments, about 400 aircraft, and one anti-aircraft artillery unit will participate, practicing joint land-air offensive and defensive battles.

Dentsu News Agency, Tokyo, 22nd: The Army Headquarters ordered the Army Aviation Headquarters to plan the first large-scale special air exercise since the founding of the Japanese air force in the eighth year of the Showa era. The final plan was decided today. The participating units are as follows: Kakamigahara Flying Regiments 1 and 2, Yokkaichi Flying Regiment 3, Tachiarai Flying Regiment 4, Tachikawa Flying Regiment 5, Hamamatsu Flying Regiment 7, Taiwan-Tung Flying Regiment 8, Tokorozawa Flying School, Shimodate Flying School, Akeno Flying School, Chiba Balloon Team, etc. Seven air regiments, three schools, and one balloon team from across the country will dispatch 400 elite aircraft, with Shizuoka, Gifu, and Aichi prefectures as the center, and Central Japan as the stage, dividing into red and white armies, and launching a great battle for Japanese airspace. The Commander-in-Chief will be General Watanabe Jōtarō, Army Councilor and Commander of the Army Aviation Headquarters. Such a large-scale air exercise is rare even in foreign countries. Since the Manchurian Incident, the importance of the air force has become increasingly apparent. In preparation for future wars, the operation and use of a large air force is of utmost importance.

National Alliance 78

Formed Party Yesterday

Kenzō Adachi Elected President

Advocates Abolition of the Cabinet System and Establishment of a State Council

Advocates Dictatorship and Economic Control

Dentsu News Agency, Tokyo, 22nd: The National Alliance held a founding ceremony at the Hibiya Public Hall at 1:00 PM today. Thirty members of the Diet belonging to Adachi, and members of both Houses, Kuan and Ōtsuka, and 1,000 party members attended. First, Kuan Naohiko was publicly elected as chairman. Dietman Izu reported the process of forming the alliance, and then the platform and covenant were declared, which were unanimously approved by the entire body. Next, the entire body unanimously elected Kenzō Adachi as president. The new President Adachi climbed onto the wall amidst applause and clapping to give an inaugural speech and encourage party members. Also, the platform decided today is as follows: (1) Adhere to the spirit of national foundation and seek the reconstruction of internationalism; (2) Establish a controlled economy and seek the guarantee of people's livelihood; (3) Eliminate the accumulated abuses in the political world and seek the thoroughness of nationalism.

Dentsu News Agency, Tokyo, 22nd: The main points of President Adachi's speech at today's founding ceremony of the National Alliance are as follows: The National Alliance is certainly inspired by the spirit of national foundation, opens up the difficult situation at home and abroad, re-establishes the foundation of an uncompromising and lasting peace, and emerges to build a society without exploitation. The National Alliance breaks away from free economic ism and takes a controlled economy as its banner, corrects the waste, chaos, and injustice of the existing economic society, so that individuals and groups can base themselves on their originality and activity to benefit the welfare of the people. The National Alliance seeks the redistribution and re-examination of national income, so that burdens are balanced and class opposition is adjusted. The biggest obstacles to improving finance and economic control are today's red tape and rules of the administrative organs. For a fundamental and major reform of the stagnation and inaction of administration, it is most important not only to break the accumulated abuses in the official world, but also to transcend the interests of party strategy. The National Alliance, in order to achieve political acumen, advocates the establishment of a State Council to abolish the cabinet system and should organize a strong political group.

China United Press, Tokyo, 22nd: The main policies announced by the National Alliance are divided into political and economic sectors. Most noteworthy is that it advocates national politics, the abolition of the cabinet system, and the establishment of a State Council in politics, and promotes an Economic Staff Headquarters and implements a controlled economy in the economy. The content is briefly described as follows:

(A) "National Politics" The former cabinet system has not only become an organ for mutually seizing budgets, but has also completely become an administrative discussion forum. Therefore, in order to implement strong (i.e., dictatorial) politics, it is necessary to first abolish the cabinet system and replace it with a State Council, so that the boundary between administration and politics is clear and complete responsibility is given. The State Council is organized by seven state ministers, divided into domestic affairs, foreign affairs, and military affairs, to deliberate on national policies, so that the heads of each province can handle affairs according to law, and new responsible heads will be placed in each province. The state ministers may also concurrently serve as the heads of the ministries of finance, foreign affairs, and national defense, in order to eliminate the ills of dual government. The State Council will also set up a Bureau of Statistics, a Bureau of Investigation, and a Bureau of Intelligence. The Diet must establish a new standing committee, with one-fifth of the Diet members serving on it. All elections will be state-run, thoroughly eliminating crimes in elections. The Ministry of Justice must be completely separated from the State Council to ensure that it is an independent organ.

(B) "Establish an Economic Staff Headquarters and Implement a Controlled Economy" The controlled economy advocated by the National Alliance is based on the control of national public interest, opposes communism, and the scope of control should be determined by the situation. (1) "Outline of Control" (i) The main commercial enterprises and banks should be controlled; (ii) Manage exchange rates and trade, and maintain a certain price level; (iii) Establish a new land system, buy up land and resell it to farmers; (iv) The state manages rice and silk; (v) Formulate an agricultural insurance law; (vi) Control the economy of Japan and Manchuria; (2) Sort out the national debt; (3) Construct a new maritime transportation policy.

Japan United News, Tokyo, 21st: The National Alliance has decided on the following committee members: President Kenzō Adachi, advisors Kuan Naohiko, Ōtake Kanichi, and Satō Kei, Secretary-General Nakano Seigō, etc.

The Northeast Problem and the League of Nations (7) 89

"Regarding the explosions that occurred on or beside the tracks between 10:00 PM and 10:30 PM on September 18th, while there is no doubt that the tracks were damaged, in reality, this did not prevent the southbound train from Changchun from arriving on time. It cannot be used as a justification for military action. Therefore, the military actions taken by the Japanese army on that night, as described in the previous section, cannot be recognized as legitimate self-defense."

This point is extremely important. If the so-called explosion near Shenyang cannot be recognized as a legitimate reason for the Japanese military actions in various nearby locations, then the military actions taken by the Japanese army in other parts of China hundreds of miles away, such as Changchun, Jilin, and Yingkou, are even less justifiable. The Japanese army attacked Chinese military camps and set them on fire, while the Chinese army was under orders not to engage in conflict with the Japanese army. This point was also mentioned in the report. The Japanese authorities spared no effort in eliminating Chinese civil officials in the three northeastern provinces, and the report also paid close attention to this. After the resolution was passed by the Council of the League of Nations on September 30th, during the effective period of the resolution, Japan intensified its efforts to destroy the power of Chinese civil officials in the three northeastern provinces. Let us examine the content of the resolution. The second section states, "The Council considers the statement of the Japanese government that it has no territorial ambitions in the Eastern Provinces to be important." The third section states, "The Council takes note of the statement by the Japanese representative that the Japanese troops have begun to withdraw and that the Japanese government will continue to withdraw its troops to within the railway zone as quickly as possible, in proportion to the certainty of guarantees for the safety of the lives and property of the Japanese people, and hopes to fully implement this desire as soon as possible." The fifth section states, "The Council takes note of the assurance by the Chinese and Japanese representatives that their respective governments will take all necessary steps to prevent the expansion of the incident or the aggravation of the situation." This resolution was accepted by Japan. However, what does the reality show us? The officials of the Liaoning Provincial Government of China, such as the acting chairman, the director of finance, the director of education, and the director of public security, were forced by the Japanese army to withdraw from Shenyang, the seat of the provincial government, and flee to Jinzhou, a city dozens of miles west of Shenyang. The report states that Japan did not allow the Chinese authorities to establish a provincial government in Jinzhou after fleeing Shenyang, and even attempted to destroy it. On October 8th, Japanese planes bombed Jiaotong University, the railway station, hospitals marked with the Red Cross, and other unarmed locations in Jinzhou, where the provincial government was located. When the Japanese planes flew low, they also strafed with machine guns. It is clear that Japan's intention was to completely eliminate the power of the Chinese authorities, which were indispensable for the organization of the government and the maintenance of law and order in southern Manchuria. After the power of the Chinese authorities in Jinzhou, Jilin, and other parts of Manchuria was eliminated one by one by the Japanese army, Japan then began to lament the lack of order in various parts of Manchuria. Japan's purpose was nothing more than to replace the Chinese authorities. This purpose,

China knows it, but Japan denies it. The League of Nations Council and General Assembly have already seen through their pretense. Japanese Prime Minister Inukai Tsuyoshi stated in December 1931 that even if China offered Manchuria as a gift, Japan would never accept it. However, at the same time, neutral news agencies such as the United Press and Reuters continuously reported the fact that the Japanese authorities were making every effort, directly or indirectly through their puppets, to seize the governing power of Manchuria. The reason why I ask you to pay special attention to the bombing of Jinzhou on October 8, 1931, and the subsequent occupation of Jinzhou and other administrative centers in Manchuria is to point out the complete lack of sincerity of the Japanese authorities. On the one hand, they intermittently obstruct the peaceful resolution of the case, and on the other hand, they trample on the League of Nations Covenant and other legal principles. The result of Japan's contempt for the dignity of the League of Nations is the untold suffering inflicted on the Chinese people. I do not wish to describe it in detail, lest I add to the unease of those present. However, I can mention a few points for your consideration. Japan first guaranteed the League of Nations on September 30th and then again on December 10th that it would not take any further action to exacerbate the situation. The so-called any action naturally includes incendiary actions that lead to bloodshed. However, guarantees are guarantees, and actions are actions. In modern Chinese history, the attack on China's territorial and administrative sovereignty has been the most egregious during this Japanese atrocity. Japan's military actions have isolated 30 million Chinese people from their compatriots. Officials in the three northeastern provinces who were loyal to the government have all been removed and replaced by Japanese puppets. The customs and salt administration organs in the three northeastern provinces have all been forcibly occupied. Post offices, telegraph lines, mines, railways, radio stations, and tax collection agencies and tax revenues have all been seized. To this day, no administrative policy can be implemented in the three northeastern provinces without the permission of the Japanese side. All of this is a manifestation of Japan's violation of its solemn guarantees to the League of Nations and its continued terrorist and assimilation policies. Paragraph 127 of the Lytton Commission Report states,

"The Japanese army, without declaring war, forcibly occupied a large portion of land that undoubtedly belonged to China, separated it from China, and declared it independent. The facts are clear. The steps taken in this process are said by Japan to be in accordance with the obligations of the League of Nations Covenant, the Kellogg-Briand Pact, and the Washington Nine-Power Treaty, but in fact, the meaning of these treaties is to prevent such actions."

Not only that, but on January 28, 1932, Japan continued to invade Chinese territory, attacking Shanghai, killing and injuring more than 24,000 Chinese people, and destroying property worth 150 million yuan in Shanghai and its surrounding areas, an unarmed city. The new Chinese army stationed in Shanghai came into contact with the Japanese army, and their resistance served as a notice to all parties concerned that the Chinese people can tolerate and adopt passive resistance to the extreme, but they can also be motivated and act with strong armed self-defense. However, even though the Japanese army encountered misfortune in Shanghai, it did not abandon its ambition. Its insistence on acting alone can be seen in its open recognition of the so-called "Manchukuo government." Japan recognized "Manchukuo" on September 14 of this year and signed a so-called protocol with the puppet organization, completely disregarding its obligations to the League of Nations Covenant and other international treaties, as well as its repeated promises to the Council. Regarding the situation in the three northeastern provinces and the recognition of "Manchukuo" by Japan, page 97 of the Investigation Team Report states,

"Therefore, the independence movement had never been heard of in Manchuria before September 1931. It is clear that this movement was only possible due to the presence of the Japanese army. Current or retired Japanese civil and military officials who are closely related to the new political movement in Japan described in Chapter 4 considered organizing and implementing this movement as a way to resolve the Manchurian situation after the September 18th Incident. These officials used the names and actions of certain Chinese people and used a small number of residents who were dissatisfied with the previous government to achieve the above-mentioned goal. The Japanese General Staff Headquarters, from the beginning or at least for a short period of time, clearly understood that this autonomy movement could be used. There is no doubt that the department provided assistance and guidance to the organizers of the independence movement. The Investigation Team is satisfied that, according to all the evidence obtained from all parties, although there are several driving forces behind the establishment of Manchukuo, the two most important are the presence of the Japanese army and the activities of Japanese civil and military officials. The combined effect of the two is the greatest. In our judgment, without these two, the new country could not have been established. Based on this reason, the current political system cannot be regarded as the product of a genuine and natural independence movement." (To be continued)

The Horrific Massacre by the Japanese Army in Fushun

American Reporter Mr. Hunter Personally Investigates 90

Not a Single One of Three Thousand Villagers Survived

All the Affected Villages Turned to Ashes

An Impartial Report from a Third Party

The Japanese Army Took Retaliatory Measures

On September 16th, the massacre of nearly 3,000 of our compatriots in Fushun by the Japanese army was confirmed on November 30th by a telegram sent to New York by Mr. Edward Hunter, a correspondent for the American International News Service, because Mr. Hunter had personally visited the site of the Fushun massacre and conducted a thorough investigation. After learning of the massacre, our government protested to the Japanese government and reported it to the League of Nations, but the Japanese government denied it. Now, we translate the foreign account as follows to show the impartial report from a third party.

The massacre of three thousand people in Fushun, men, women, old and young, without exception, is a confirmed fact. I am now returning to that place, seeing its prosperity, which is due to the wealth obtained from the world's largest open-pit coal mine. After inspecting the surrounding area, I found that the houses there were all burned by the Japanese army, and the residents were gathered in one place by the Japanese army and massacred with machine guns, which was extremely miserable. Everything was witnessed by me and heard from the refugees, and the evidence is conclusive and undeniable. The remaining brick and mud walls of the affected villages, pointing to the sky, were blackened by the fire, like outstretched, tragic arms. The beams of the houses were all turned to ashes. The Chinese farmers, workers, and women and children who survived in the affected villages all described the event in the same way. After arriving at the place, the Japanese army treated the villagers like livestock, driving them into the pens where livestock were kept, and then taking them to a nearby hillside and massacring them. At the same time, they set fire to the villagers' homes with kerosene.

Why Did the Japanese Army Take This Action? 91

Why did the Japanese army take this measure? The answer is the same: it was a retaliatory measure by the Japanese side against the villagers. In mid-September, the volunteer army that attacked Fushun had passed through the area. This attack caused the Japanese side to lose 350,000 yuan and kill several Japanese people. Therefore, retaliatory measures were taken against the villages here. However, even the Japanese side admitted that the volunteer army did not come from the villages massacred by the Japanese army this time, but from the Red Spear Society in Xinbin County, 40 miles east of Fushun, which was organized by simple-minded people. The weapons they used were red-tasseled spears. This is a secret organization formed by the people themselves.

Blood Flowed Like Rivers, Turning the Ground Red 92

I stood on a steep hillside, which happened to be the center of the surrounding massacre of farmers, so I could see everything clearly. I only saw fragments of the farmers' clothes worn by the massacred farmers and women and children, stained with blood, scattered at the massacre site. Everywhere I looked, there were newly raised mounds, all new graves. What I smelled with my nose confirmed that the place was a massacre site. A farmer mustered the courage to follow me to the place, because there was a cottage a mile away from the massacre site, where a Japanese woman lived. There was a telephone in the house. If the Japanese woman saw someone at the massacre site, she would notify the Japanese military police in Fushun. Therefore, the villagers regarded it as a dangerous road. This cottage may be inhabited by dead souls, because it is the only one that has not been burned.

Villages in a Dangerous Area 93

The first village in the affected villages is located within an 8-mile radius of the Fushun Station of the South Manchuria Railway, but it is extremely difficult to reach the village because it is a dangerous area. All foreign consulates have banned foreigners from going there. The Japanese and "Manchukuo" officials also intend to cut off its external transportation. At the end of the Fushun coal mine, there is a gate surrounded by barbed wire. This gate is opened during the day to allow Chinese miners to return to their nearby villages. The affected Qianjinpu Village is about several miles away. On the way to Qianjinpu, one must first wade across a semi-frozen river. The village is located on the right side of the road and can be seen at a glance. When I went to the place, the scenery of the village revealed a desolate and miserable scene. The villages in China are usually very noisy, but this place was silent, like a grave. There was not a single man, woman, or child. The ashes of the burned beams filled the wide space surrounded by the walls blackened by the fire. The tragic situation of all the houses was the same. I entered a certain affected house and walked on the broken tiles on the roof, the curved kerosene drums (which the people used as water buckets), and the broken kitchen god. The wells of each house also showed the same tragic situation, without a single survivor. A two-wheeled cart lost one wheel, and the other wheel was burned. The heavy stone mortar, which is a necessity for the family, was also destroyed and mixed with the burned wood. Along this dead village and the frozen river, only crows were miserably hidden in the chimneys. The above is the road I traveled.

Exchanging News of the Tragedy 94

As I advanced, pedestrians stopped and exchanged information about the Fushun massacre. Everyone had their own experiences. For example, Mr. Dong lost his two sisters, but fortunately his parents were safe. Although the total number of deaths and injuries was nearly 3,000, only 200 people died in his village, because it was closest to the city and received the news of the Japanese army's arrival earlier. Mr. Dong pointed to the four black walls and said that the owner of this house did not heed his advice to escape, and both husband and wife died. They fled with those who had difficulty escaping in the evening, and Japanese planes dropped bombs on their heads, but the damage was less than arson and machine guns. There were about 400 households in his village. The Japanese army was stationed in the surrounding mountains, so there was no way to escape. The villagers were all driven to the foot of the mountain by the Japanese army, unable to see their homes. Then the Japanese army set fire and burned the entire village, and all the villagers were killed.

Disciplined Destruction 95

Looking around, I saw that the Japanese side carried out its cruel retaliation based on a precise training, the accuracy of which was like the train of the South Manchuria Railway. They were not bandits, because no family was spared, and no house in the area was spared. Even those hundreds of yards away, and whose destruction would require great effort, were not spared. Not a single roof was spared. All vehicles were broken or burned. Not even chickens and dogs were left. The situation was the same in a certain village slightly farther away from the village. This village was a prosperous brick kiln area. Now only the remaining bricks remain. The walls around the homes of the kiln owners and workers were sloping. When I entered these houses and met people, they would point me to the places where their friends and relatives died. "An old lady was crushed by the burning beams and could not escape, so she turned to ashes." "There was Aunt Shen, who did not want to leave, so she was burned to death on the stove." It is difficult to describe such terrible tragedies. The Fushun area was not limited to the above three villages. The Japanese army massacred nine villages. According to my investigation, the village of Datongjia, 10 miles south of Fushun, was also massacred by the Japanese army in the same way six days before the volunteer army attacked Fushun. All of this can be collectively called the Fushun massacre. My news was obtained from personal visits in dangerous environments and from conversations with affected villagers. About two weeks before the Fushun attack by the volunteer army, 14 Japanese soldiers ate in the village of Datongchow. When they left the village, they were suddenly attacked. Four people were killed and the rest escaped. The farmers said that it was not done by the villagers. Later, six Japanese cars came and stopped in the nearby Mengjiakou Village for a considerable period of time, burning three houses. According to the farmers, when they arrived in Datongzhou Village, 20 men, women, and children on the street were

Page 10

Killed by Japanese soldiers with bayonets and bullets. Japanese planes dropped bombs in the surrounding area and destroyed the houses in Mengjiakou Village. The next day, the Japanese army returned to Datongzhou Village and burned 100 houses in the village, burning more than 20 livestock to death. The above was told to me by a young man living in a nearby village, whose uncle was also one of the victims. His uncle's son escaped and recounted the incident. According to the villagers, about 6,000 Red Spear Society members and volunteer soldiers came from Xin , 40 miles away, to attack Fushun. They attacked in three routes. The middle route went to the south of Fushun, and the rest attacked from the sides on the left and right wings. Only the middle route entered Fushun. They attacked at 11:00 PM and the whole city was awakened from their dreams by the shouting. They fled at 3:00 AM. The Japanese army that came from Shenyang only had 600 people, so they did not dare to pursue, but they carried out organized retaliatory massacres on the villages through which the three routes of the volunteer army passed.

Machine Guns Used as Cameras 96

The right wing of the Red Spear Society retreated south through Pingdingshan and Lizigou, Litsekow. There were 6,000 households in these two places. According to the refugees and residents of the area, the thousands of residents summoned by the Japanese army were gathered on a hillside. Mr. Dong said, "My village is eight miles away from there. When I heard the noise and ran outside, I saw a person named Fu running madly towards me, covered in blood, but fortunately not injured. His face was pale, and he told me in a hurried voice about the massacre he had narrowly escaped. First, Japanese soldiers came to his house and forced him to carry his old mother to the hillside. The Japanese soldiers then ordered everyone gathered there not to leave the hillside without permission, because they would search for the Red Spear Society. All the nearby areas that were considered to be part of the Red Spear Society had been killed, and their houses had all been burned. Then, the Japanese soldiers told them that they were going to take pictures, but there were no cameras at that time, no lenses, only machine guns and bullets. Mr. Fu said that his old mother was the first to be killed. When he fell, his mother's body pressed down on him. Suddenly, a Korean shouted, 'The Japanese have retreated, you can stand up.' He was fortunate enough to be unable to stand up at that time. All those who stood up were shot down by the second machine gun fire. All those who were kicked and moved, and children, were stabbed with guns. Mr. Fu was stained with his mother's blood, so he pretended to be dead and escaped. Because a unit of the volunteer army failed to enter Fushun and fled to these villages, the village suffered the most severe punishment. I have personally witnessed the three villages in the central part, Hailindun, Yangpaipu Yangpaipu, and Qianjinpu. Each village had 100 households. Before the Red Spear Society attacked, the Japanese army had built a defense line here. According to the farmers, the Japanese army used the fact that these three villages had failed to force the volunteer army to advance as a pretext for retaliation, and the Japanese army was divided into many small teams, each team dealing with a number of households. When I witnessed it, the retaliatory work had been completed. All the residents who were hiding in the houses had been burned to death. The three villages in the west, namely Andukiao Ertaokov Qianjiaotiaotze, or Hejiaotiaotze Huvkvchiatze, suffered less damage. Seven households were burned in Qian Village and three households in He Village. After the massacre, the Chinese police self-defense force and the volunteer army rebelled. According to reports for several weeks, after the cruel massacre, the Red Spear Society still attacked Fushun, but on a smaller scale, so although gunshots could be heard in the city, there were no losses.

Inspection Report on the Suppression of Communists and the Recovery of Various Areas (5)

Inspection of the Communist Bandit Stronghold of Honghu 97

A reporter accompanied the inspection group, arriving at Xindi from Jianli at 8:30 PM on the 13th. The following morning, they boarded an armored motorboat used for suppressing bandits in Honghu and went to inspect the bandit stronghold. They spent two days inspecting Honghu and returned to Xindi on the afternoon of the 15th. On the morning of the 16th, they left Xindi and returned to Hankou. The findings of the Honghu inspection are recorded below:

(The Situation of Honghu) Honghu was originally Wenxiang County. Due to vicissitudes and changes, the land submerged and became a lake, then was reassigned to Mianyang. The lake is 47 li long and approximately 39 li wide. The total area of the lake is estimated to be 1,064 square li. It is a vast expanse of water, seemingly endless. The surrounding area is crisscrossed by rivers, with numerous streams and tributaries, narrow roads, and dense reeds. The terrain is treacherous, no less than the Liangshan Marsh in the Song Dynasty. It is a place to harbor filth and hide criminals, a natural den of bandits. Even before the Communist bandits occupied the lake, bandits and thieves roamed there, causing trouble for the people. The government authorities ignored this issue and never suppressed them. The Communist bandits seized the opportunity to rise up and occupy it as their stronghold, eventually becoming a major threat.

(The Origin of the Communist Bandits) In 1927, Communist Party members Xu Xu, Lou Minxiu, Peng Guocai, Liu Xiafeng, and Li Gongyi from Mianyang and Jianli counties began to operate in the Honghu area. Under the guise of overthrowing local tyrants, they implemented terrorist tactics, secretly expanding their influence. After the purge of the Communist Party, most of them surrendered. However, a few members, including Lou Minxiu, hid along the lake shore and waited for an opportunity to act. Lou was a native of Mianyang city, as fair-skinned as a woman. He was gentle and refined in his youth, praised by the villagers. After joining the Communist Party, he completely changed his old ways and became a different person. In the winter of 1928, when the stationed troops were transferred, Lou went to Qujiawan, gathered Communist bandits from Jianli and Mianyang, and organized the Red Army, claiming to be the commander-in-chief. They had three or four guns and forty or fifty followers. On the eve of the lunar New Year, taking advantage of the fact that the military and civilians were busy celebrating the New Year, they went out to rob. They stealthily went to the Liuguan and Zhuhe areas and adopted the methods of Liangshan heroes, such as attacking homes, stealing camps, and seizing fortresses. They plundered police firearms and searched for civilian property. The military and police were unprepared and were often taken by surprise. They captured four or five hundred rifles, and their momentum gradually increased. They then stealthily went to the Jiangling area and repeated their tactics. By early February 1929, they had returned to Qujiawan with more than 1,000 rifles and more than 2,000 people. Duan Dechang was appointed as the fake military commander. Duan was a native of Huarong and had served as the director of the Political Department of the 8th Division of Tang Shengzhi's army. He was courageous, extremely cunning, and familiar with the Water Margin. Every time he plundered, he changed the established methods and applied them, often deceiving the local military and police. After Duan arrived in Qujiawan, he made some arrangements and launched a second attack, going to the Lizhou and Jinshi areas of Hunan. He joined forces with the bandit leader He Long and formed two armies. He was appointed as the fake commander-in-chief, Kuang Jixun was appointed as the fake commander of the Second Army, and Duan Dechang was appointed as the fake commander of the Sixth Army. He was a native of western Hunan, with a background as an outlaw. He was fierce and unparalleled. During the Northern Expedition, he served as the commander of the 40th Army. After the purge of the Communist Party, he became a bandit. Kuang Jixun was from Sichuan and a graduate of the Huangpu Military Academy with military knowledge. In July 1929, He, Duan, Kuang and others led the bandit troops to Qujiawan and held a mass meeting. They established fake military and political organs in Qu. From then on, the Communist bandit forces in the central Hubei area began to grow, and they invaded and occupied Jianli, Fengkou, Xiantao, and Shishou. In November of that year, after being suppressed by the National Army, the bandits were defeated and scattered. The lost areas were completely recovered, and the National Army pursued them directly to Qujiawan. In December, the National Army returned to Mianyang for some reason, and the bandit forces revived. The recovered areas were again lost. The bandits then carried out massacres everywhere, and blood flowed into the ditches. From then on, their power became more and more rampant and gradually spread to the north bank of Xiang River, almost out of control.

(Organization of the Communist Bandits) The Communist bandits in the central Hubei area were meticulously organized. In terms of party and government, they had the "Hunan-Hubei-West Provincial Committee of the Communist Party of China" and "County, District, and Township Committees," as well as the "Hunan-Hubei-West Soviet" and "County, District, and Township Soviets." In terms of military affairs, they organized a "Military Commission" to discuss major military plans. In addition to the Red Army, they also selected strong young men to organize the Red Guards and the Young Pioneers to be used by them. There were also organizations such as the Security Bureau, the Trade Union, the Farmers' Association, and the Women's Team. The Communist Party's fake Hunan-Hubei-West Provincial Committee had one secretary who had overall authority, Yang Zhishan. It had departments for publications, propaganda, organization, and women. The Propaganda Minister was Zong Panming, the Organization Minister was Yang Chenglin, and the Women's Minister was Zhang Xiaogui. The secretary was Sister Wang, and there was also a secretariat with various departments. The fake Hunan-Hubei-West Soviet had a presidium of nine people, consisting of Cui Qi, Ma Wu, He Long, Duan Dechang, Peng Zhiyu, Li Jiafen, Zhou Meitong, and others. Cui Qi was the chairman. It was divided into departments for internal affairs, economic finance, land, labor, justice, unemployment services, and others. The fake Military Commission consisted of He Long, Duan Dechang, Kuang Jixun, and others. The fake Provincial Committee, the Provincial Soviet, the Military Commission, the General Trade Union, the Farmers' Association, and other organs were all located in Qujiawan. The Mianyang County Soviet was located in Fengkou, and the Li-Jian County Soviet was located in Zhuhe. Other organs were established in the provinces, counties, districts, and townships, depending on the nature of the province and county. The organization was extremely complex and meticulous.

(Construction of the Bandit Stronghold) The Communist bandits in Honghu used Xindi as a port to secretly communicate and transport goods with the outside world. After several years of operation, the bandit stronghold had an armory and a mint for making guns and money. It had a very large radio station to communicate with the outside world. It established several hospitals that could accommodate thousands of wounded bandit soldiers and set up a Lenin School to carry out communist education. There was also a Lenin warship for naval warfare. The scale was grand and could not be compared with ordinary small bandits. (To be continued)

A Record of Inspection in Yexian After the Robbery 98

Broken wells, dilapidated walls, a pile of rubble

A century of essence destroyed in one battle

A dispatch from Jinan: Since September 16, Han Fuju mobilized tens of thousands of troops to denounce Liu Zhentian. Liu's troops concentrated in Yexian, holding the city to resist. The Han army, considering the lives and property of the people in the city, did not actively attack, only surrounding it with heavy troops. The siege lasted for two months without resolution. Later, after the central government sent officials to Shandong to mediate, the Han army lifted the siege and withdrew west of the Wei River on November 12. Liu's army was also ordered to leave Shandong within a time limit and transferred to eastern Zhejiang. Liu's army in Yexian began to move on the 17th of last month, heading to Yantai in stages and boarding ships to go south. By the 9th of this month, the departure was completed. The provincial committee's county magistrate, public security chief, and others entered the city on the 10th to take over. In order to understand the state of local destruction and the situation after the robbery, the reporter took the time to go to Yexian on the 17th to inspect everything. Now, the findings of the inspection will be described below to inform the readers.

Order Restored on the Yantai-Weixian Road 99

The reporter left Ji'nan on the 17th and stayed overnight in Weixian that night. On the Yantai-Weixian road, although it had suffered a major military event, it had never stopped traffic, except for the most tense days when the provincial army was advancing east. During the siege of Yexian, the Weixian-Shahe road was still open to military traffic. After the army retreated, the traffic area also gradually expanded, but it could not be opened to the Liu army's area because they would detain any vehicles they saw. When the reporter went to Yexian, traffic had reached Longkou. Now that Liu's army in Yantai has all boarded ships, it is planned to open the traffic directly to Yantai today or tomorrow. However, when the military operation started, all the vehicles in the eastern section were detained and used by Liu's army. There are only twelve vehicles left, and several are old and unusable. There are few cars and many passengers, so it is very crowded. But at this time when the military has just ended and people's hearts have not yet been stabilized, the road has been able to return to normal, which is very rare.

Roadbed Destroyed, Station Burned 100

The reporter's car departed at 8:30 and arrived in Yexian at 12:00. The road was relatively smooth and there were no major problems. The Xinhe Changqiao Bridge, which had been burned, has not yet been repaired, and several charred trees still stand in the center of the river. When the car arrived in the area of ​​Wulihouzi and Shilipu, the trenches and ramparts built by the provincial army could be seen, winding through the fields and remaining intact. Because the car was traveling very fast, there was no opportunity to observe carefully. When the car arrived about a li away from Yexian, it could not move forward, because this section of the road, which was more than 900 meters long, circled the northwest corner of Yexian City in a semi-circular shape. At that time, Liu's army dug battle trenches on this section of the road. Now the road bureau is recruiting many workers to actively fill them in, but it has not been completely completed. The newly filled soil is very loose, and the car travels on it with great difficulty. Passengers must get out of the car and walk. The car station outside the North Gate of Yexian was located on the front line of the Liu army's first line of defense, and had been demolished and burned to ashes. Now the station is temporarily borrowing a surviving ancient temple as a temporary station in order to handle traffic affairs.

Trenches and Ramparts Startling to the Eye 101

After the reporter got off the car, he walked into the city and crossed the Liu army's trenches and ramparts outside the North Gate. This place was the main line of defense of the Liu army. The cross-section of this defensive line was also half a li wide. The barbed wire in the front row was still completely hanging on the posts. Behind it, several steps away, were caltrops, broken branches, and messy firewood, hindering passage. In front of the caltrops were landmines, bombs, electric mines, and other things. Although the Liu army had dug up a lot of them when they retreated, there were still many left. Until now, no one dared to go there. Behind the caltrops was the outer moat, which was both deep and wide, intended to prevent the enemy from trespassing. Behind the outer moat was the lying trench, which was deep enough to accommodate people. Soldiers would either lie or sit in it, holding guns to defend. Behind the lying trench was the communication trench, which was winding and twisting, passing through various places, for soldiers to advance and retreat and transport bullets and supplies. Further back was the covered trench, which was covered with wooden boards, tree branches, and other things, and covered with soil on top. Behind the covered trench was the shelter, which looked like a dungeon, either square or round, or in an irregular shape, all connected to the covered trench. It was for accommodation, rest, and storage of military supplies. Now most of them have been demolished, because the wooden boards and other materials used were mostly doors, windows, boxes, and cabinets from civilian homes, which have been taken away by the owners. This defense line was arranged in layers, which was very spectacular. It surrounded the city for dozens of li, and restoring this trench was a very large project.

Four Gates Decayed, A Pile of Rubble 102

The destruction was most severe in the four gates, especially in the Huayuangou and Gelili streets of the East Gate. All the buildings were turned into rubble and ashes, with no complete rooms. The best ones had only four walls standing, but they were as rare as morning stars. According to the disaster victims, the reason why these places were so devastated was not because of artillery fire, but because the Liu army demolished the beams and pillars of each house in order to clear the line of sight and prevent the provincial army from using them for cover and stealthy advance, and then set them on fire, turning them into flat ground. In addition, the areas of Dongyingfang and Beiyao in the northeast corner of the city were also destroyed as described above. The South Gate and the North Gate were slightly less damaged, but they were also ten empty houses out of ten, with almost no four walls left. It was heard that the troops searched everywhere, leaving no place untouched. Fearing that the people would bury valuables, they dug everywhere, and no one was spared. Every household had no doors, looking like ruins and broken kilns. Until now, there was no smoke from cooking. Bricks and tiles were piled up everywhere, and the desolate situation was shocking. The walls of each house were connected to each other, like a main road. Those who returned from refuge only piled up bricks and tiles to temporarily serve as doors, and inserted branches and hung reeds to divide the courtyards. Those who did not clean up remained in their original state, allowing people to pay their respects.

Refugees Seek Lost Possessions with Tears 103

When the reporter entered the city, there were many sacks of earth and bricks piled up inside and outside the city gate. The situation at that time can be imagined. The destruction inside the city was very different from the four gates. The houses along the street were relatively intact, but the interiors were also empty, with only four walls left. The digging situation was the same as in the four gates. Now most of the residents have found their doors and installed them, making them look a little neater. Speculative merchants have brought scattered items from outside to set up stalls and sell them, so the intersection of the streets has gradually become lively. The doors, windows, wood, boxes, cabinets, and other items that were collected by the Liu army to build trenches and ramparts, now that the Liu army has retreated, if the people are allowed to dig them out automatically, it is feared that disputes will be unavoidable. Therefore, the street chiefs sent people to dig them out and concentrate them in one place, allowing people to sign for their original belongings. Therefore, at every street and alley, there were often piles of doors, windows, boxes, cabinets, and other items like mountains. Dozens of refugees wandered among them with tears and sobs, each looking for their lost items. The tragic and desolate scene was unbearable to witness.

Piles of Corpses Waiting to Be Buried 104

In this battle, according to the Public Security Bureau's investigation, thirty-six men and women civilians died directly from artillery fire in the city, and forty-three were injured. Forty-nine people died and five were injured in the four gates. A hasty investigation is unavoidable and may have left out information. The exact number should be more than this. In addition, there were about 700 people who died from shock, arson, and women who committed suicide after being raped. There were also hundreds of corpses left by the Liu army, all scattered and abandoned. Many were still exposed. Those who had been buried were also buried very shallowly and urgently needed to be buried deeply. Fortunately, it was winter. If it were summer, an epidemic would break out, which would be unimaginable. Now the Public Security Bureau is sending police to actively bury them in order to prevent snow and ice from making the work more difficult. (To be continued)

Delineation of Boundaries of Li Huang County 105

To establish special district

Under direct control of Headquarters

Dispatch from Hankou: The Commander-in-Chief's Headquarters, in view of the fact that Wei Lihuang's troops recovered the bandit's den of Jinjiazhai, in order to facilitate control, specially changed it to a county seat, and named the county Li Huang, to honor the achievements. As for the boundaries of the county, Zheng Yangwu was appointed, together with representatives from the governments of the three provinces of Henan, Hubei, and Anhui, to conduct a survey and delineation. At the beginning of this month, Zheng, the Hubei representative Huang Houyan, the Anhui representative Liu Yunqing, the Henan representative, and the county magistrates of Huoshan, Liuan, Huoqiu, Shangcheng, Gushi, and other counties arrived in Jinjiazhai. After several days of meetings, they surveyed the map and decided to use the natural terrain of the mountains and rivers as the boundary. The areas to be carved out from Anhui province are seventeen Bao from Liuan county, namely Mabao Bao, Shibabao Shang Bao, Shibabao Xia Bao, Da Xiaoyu Shang Bao, Da Xiaoyu Xia Bao, Que Shang Bao, Que Xia Bao, Su Shang Bao, Su Xia Bao, Badahu Bao, Maoping Bao, Xindian Bao, Huaishuzhen Bao, Gubeichong Bao, Nanzhuangban Bao, Huangshihe Bao, Yufutan Bao, Tongtaoyuan Bao, Xiangshansi Bao, Caixialing Bao, Changshanchong Bao; Huoqiu County to cede three Bao, namely Baliwan Bao, Kaishunjie Bao, Baitajie Bao; The areas to be carved out from Henan province are two and a half Bao from Gushi county, namely Jinzhai Bao, Liqiao Bao, Changjianghe half Bao; Shangcheng County to cede fourteen and a half Bao, namely Foshang Bao, Fozhong Bao, Foxia Bao, Zhushang Bao, Zhuxia Bao, Xishang Bao, Xizhong Bao, Xixia Bao, Wangzhenzhai Bao, Shuanghe Bao, Qingshang Bao, Qingxia Bao, Mengshang Bao, Mengxia Bao, Xuan Shang half Bao, totaling forty-five Bao in the entire territory. As for the boundaries of Hubei province, because the Tongluoguan, Changlingguan, and Jieling mountain ranges bordering Anhui province are the main watersheds, the terrain is natural, and it was decided not to include them. The results of the survey were reported to the Headquarters for approval on the 20th. As to which province it should belong to, the opinions of the garrison commanders and county magistrates were also consulted, and it was considered appropriate to assign it to Anhui province. Zheng and others, however, believe that it is far from the provinces of Henan and Anhui, and political facilities may be beyond reach, and have suggested that it be designated as a special district directly under the Command Headquarters for bandit suppression. (December 21)

Xu and He's Remnant Bandits Fleeing Separately 106

He Chengjun will return to Hankou and immediately go to Shaanxi to supervise the suppression.

The remaining bandits in eastern and northern Hubei still need to be eliminated.

Dispatch from Hankou: Xu and He's remnant bandits, who had fled from Hubei to Shaanxi, were difficult to secure due to the blockade and suppression by the National Army, and then turned back and fled south. Xu's forces were recently in the areas south of Chenggu County, including Erlangba, Sunjiaping, Siduhe, and Zhongjiagou. He's bandits fled to the Bashan Mountains on the border of Shaanxi and Sichuan. The bandits were severely damaged and suffered heavy losses. They also attempted to break up into smaller units in order to preserve some of their strength. The separation of Xu and He from the union was also inevitable. The National Army decided to completely annihilate Xu's bandit forces first, as they had more followers. The troops entering Shaanxi included Liu Maoen, Hu Zongnan, and Xiao Zhichu's troops. Liu's troops are now moving from Baocheng to Xinjihuangguanling to prevent further westward escape. Hu's division crossed the river from Hanzhong and followed up to Dapanba Jingpoba. Xiao's division advanced from Tiexingba, Guankouzhen, Huoditang, and to Qinggeng Wuliba. Zhao and Wang's brigades of the Shaanxi army are also advancing towards Sunjiaping Songmeng'an. Earlier, when Xu's bandits fled west, they were as fast as the wind. Along the way, the weather was cold, so they plundered civilian clothes to keep warm. Because the National Army penetrated deep into Shaanxi, the transportation of military uniforms was delayed, and they did not want to take from the people, so they marched through the snow, enduring great hardship. Therefore, the bandits were able to drive straight in, and the chasing troops were further away from the bandit forces. It was not until the bandits fled south that they were able to intercept them. Recently, they have just completed the encirclement. However, the main force of the bandits still has several thousand men. Xu Xiangqian, Kuang Jixun, and others are all in the army. Although Liu, Hu, and Xiao's troops of the National Army are all elite troops, the strength of the Shaanxi army is weaker. Whether they can be wiped out in one fell swoop depends on the efforts of the armies. He Chengjun, who was ordered to enter Shaanxi to supervise the suppression, had previously gone to Beijing to attend the Third Plenary Session. On the 21st, he returned to Hankou from Beijing by plane. He will go to Shaanxi to supervise the troops within a few days, and set up a branch office in Xi'an. However, He's old illness has not been cured. According to him, he still needs to stay in Hankou for a few days to recuperate before he can go. It is expected that Yang Hucheng will first depart for the front to take command in person, while He will be stationed in Xi'an to preside over everything. As for the Xu and He's remnant bandits who are hiding in Hubei, the bandits have not been eliminated. In the Huangma area in eastern Hubei, scattered bandits appear from time to time, cutting off the roads. North of Huang'an, up to the border of Henan, there are even more scattered bandits. Therefore, the bandit area inspection team heard this and retreated. That place is a place where bandits such as Xu and Kuang have been operating for a long time. Most of the people have been communist-ized. When the army comes, they are good people. When the army leaves, they become bandits again. When there are many soldiers, they are as tame as sheep. When there are few soldiers, they rise up and seize weapons. Therefore, eliminating scattered bandits after the recovery of the bandit area is still an important issue. In northern Hubei, near Fang County, there is a remnant of He's bandits lurking. Recently, taking advantage of the withdrawal of the Sichuan army, they crossed the river and fled south, attempting to return to the old nest of Shihe. However, it is an organized group, and the guns are not necessarily sufficient, so suppression will be easier. In addition, Kong's bandits in southern Hubei have not been eradicated. That place has been assigned to the command of Zhu Shaoliang, the commander-in-chief of the Xiang-E-Gan border area, for suppression. Zhu has recently ordered a general attack. Guo Rudong, the commander of the 26th Division, led his troops to Yangxin Town, 30 li away from Longgang. Zhang Gang, the commander of the security regiment, led his troops to Cikou to carry out suppression. Rong Jingfang, the commander of the 81st Division, was stationed near Jinniu Taipingtang to intercept them. Xie Bin, the commander of the 85th Division, was stationed in Tongshan, responsible for guerrilla warfare and responding to all sides. Kong's bandits were defeated in successive battles and have fled to the border area of ​​Xiang-Gan. (December 21)

Shandong Provincial Government Hastening to Handle the Aftermath in Jiaodong 107

First allocate 20,000 yuan to relieve the three counties of Yexian, Laiyang, and Qixia

Li Shuchun will personally inspect the counties in Jiaodong

Dispatch from Jinan: In this Han-Liu war, the counties in Jiaodong suffered from the ravages of war, especially Yexian, Laiyang, and Qixia. The disaster victims have no clothes or food, and many of their houses have been destroyed. They are sleeping in the ice and snow, crying from hunger and cold, which is very pitiful. The provincial government had long intended to find ways to provide relief, but because Liu's army had not been completely withdrawn, the situation was restrictive and they could not start. Yesterday, they received a telegram from Gao Lingbai, the commissioner monitoring the withdrawal of troops, from Yantai, saying that Liu's division could be withdrawn by the 22nd. The magistrate of Yexian County, Zhao Hongze, and the people of various counties have also sent telegrams, requesting relief. Today (the 20th), the provincial government's standing committee decided to first allocate 20,000 yuan from the provincial treasury and hand it over to Li Shuchun, the director of the Department of Civil Affairs, to go to the three counties of Yexian, Laiyang, and Qixia to provide relief as appropriate. The Departments of Civil Affairs and Finance will also properly draft fundraising and relief measures. Han Fuju will also donate three months' salary to provide relief to the disaster victims in Jiaodong. It is heard that Li Shuchun will depart from Ji'nan by armored train at 8:00 AM on the 22nd, arrive in Weixian on the same day, and transfer to a car to Changyi. The next day, he will go to Yexian to inspect and provide relief. After that, he will take the Yantai-Weixian line and go to Longkou, Huangxian, Penglai, Fushan, and Qixia counties to inspect. On the way back, he will go to Laiyang Pingdu again. If time permits, he will also go to Muping Rongcheng Wenjue three counties. But he must rush back before the Gregorian New Year. The departments and the secretariat will each send one person to accompany him. Chen Weixin, the director of the Yantai-Weixian Automobile Road Bureau, will also accompany Li Dong to inspect the road and plan for repairs (traffic between Weixian and Longkou has now returned to normal). The provincial government's standing committee's resolution on providing relief to the counties in Jiaodong is recorded below: "Proposal" The secretariat reports that Zhao Hongze, the magistrate of Yexian County, wrote a letter stating that during this military operation, Yexian was occupied by the military. The merchants in the four gates were looted, and although the city suffered less damage, most of them were also robbed. It is now estimated that there are more than 4,000 disaster victims. Fortunately, the Red Swastika Society is providing temporary relief to avoid freezing and starvation. However, the severe winter is long and spring plowing is hopeless. If there is no large amount of funds to inject into long-term relief, thousands of disaster victims will inevitably starve to death. The magistrate has witnessed the tragic situation and is very sad. I hereby report and request that relief funds be allocated and relief be provided as soon as possible to save the disaster victims, and so on. How should this be handled? Please make a public decision. "Resolution" First, allocate 20,000 yuan from the provincial treasury and hand it over to Committee Member Li Shuchun to go to the three counties of Yexian, Laiyang, and Qixia to provide relief as appropriate. As for the fundraising method, the Department of Civil Affairs and the Department of Finance will draft a detailed report and reply. (December 20)

Songjiang

All Circles Promoting the Construction of Dr. Sun Yat-sen Memorial 108

Our county has previously proposed by the County District Party Department, to build the Dr. Sun Yat-sen Memorial Monument at the base of the Yuecheng in the West Gate. The residents of that place were willing to give up the land, to bring the construction to fruition. The Bureau of Construction drafted a plan and submitted it to the Department of Construction, which was approved by the provincial government. The Bureau was instructed to actively handle the matter. Then, the Department of Construction ordered the Memorial Monument to be moved to the Jade Emperor Pavilion, and the base of the Yuecheng in the West Gate to be reserved for public construction. The changes in government orders have caused confusion among the people. Now, various institutions have organized the Songjiang All Circles Construction Dr. Sun Yat-sen Memorial Monument Committee, to work together and ensure its completion. Yesterday, a meeting was held at the County Party Department. Representatives from the County Government, the County Party Department, the Bureau of Finance, Public Security, Education, Construction, the District Office, the Property Office, and the County Chamber of Commerce attended. Party Committee Member Wang Zhe was elected as the chairman. After discussion, it was decided that the name of the committee would be the Songjiang All Circles Construction Dr. Sun Yat-sen Memorial Monument Committee. It was decided that the central location of the Yuecheng in the West Gate would be the location for the construction of the monument. The committee will send a letter to the County Party Department and the County Government to report to the province for filing. The construction cost of the monument will be discussed again after the County Government replies to the meeting according to the previous agreed method. The committee will send a letter to the Bureau of Construction, requesting it to create a model of the monument and provide a cost estimate based on the revised red line drawings from the Department of Construction. The County Party Department will be publicly elected to preside over the committee and affairs, and the standing committee will be held twice a month.

Party and Government Send Personnel to Inspect Movies 109

The entertainment industry in our county is developing rapidly. The Party and Government Talks Committee decided to implement the Ministry of Interior's method of inspecting movies. The County Party Department designated Propaganda Officer Zhang Longshi as the instructor, and the Public Security Bureau sent Zeng Lin and the Education Bureau sent Wang Dunshu as movie inspectors. The inspection will be implemented immediately.

Suzhou

Robbery and Murder Near Mudu 110

Sun Shuigen's family, who opened the Meiyuan teahouse in Changhong, five li away from Mudu Town in Suzhou Township, was suddenly visited by seven bandits on the night of the 21st. They looted at will and left fully loaded. Before leaving, they shot and wounded Sun Shuigen's wife and daughter, and shot and killed a neighboring Mao family girl. That night, the captain of the 7th Water Police Team led a team to sweep the area, but the bandits had disappeared.

Wuxi

Prisoner Who Illegally Manufactured Poison Pills Escorted to the Provincial Capital 111

Yang Xianyi's second daughter, Yang Lanying, who opened a smoking den in Sibaobao Bridge Alley outside the North Gate, previously demanded 200 silver dollars worth of opium from her younger brother but was refused. She then reported to the county court and had her father, Yang Xianyi, arrested and detained. It was discovered that Yang Lanying was also running an operation to sell opium and red pills. Her younger brother found out and was enraged, so he reported it to the County Public Security Bureau. Director Wu, upon receiving the report, immediately dispatched a detective team to the address. They apprehended Yang Lanying on the spot and seized two iron boxes. One box was full of opium, and the other was full of red pills. They were all taken to the bureau. Yesterday, they were presented to the county government for interrogation. Chief Wang opened the court for questioning. According to Yang Lanying's confession, the opium and red pills were bought by her late husband. Her husband was addicted to opium and red pills, and his addiction was severe. He passed away years ago. She also smokes because of her illness and begs the court to be lenient. Chief Wang reviewed the confession and, considering the seriousness of the case, ordered her detention pending escort to the provincial capital for further interrogation. At the same time, County Magistrate Chen submitted a document to the Civil Affairs Department for strict handling of Lu Fenglin and Li Zhengyang, the two principal offenders arrested by the Sixteenth Branch of the Anzhen Public Security Bureau in Yangjian Town for illegally manufacturing poison pills.

Passenger from Jiangyin Commits Suicide in Wuxi 112

A passenger from Jiangyin arrived at Mengyuan Inn on Tongyun Road on the morning of the day before yesterday. He was wearing a short blue cloth coat and looked like a worker. He claimed to be named He Zhongyan, 23 years old, and worked at a pharmacy in Jiangyin. The porter booked him room number 27. Unexpectedly, after He booked the room, he secretly took red arsenic to commit suicide. The inn noticed and, fearing implication due to his death in the inn, gave him ten silver dollars and told him to leave. He then went to Tianbao Warehouse under Jixiang Bridge and booked room number 5. Yesterday morning, He's poisoning took effect, and he moaned softly. The warehouse was shocked and immediately ordered the porter to move him to the public area of the inn while notifying his younger brother, He Zhongxian. Around noon, he died. Later, He Zhongxian, along with the local leader Xi Zhiliang, reported the matter to the county court. Prosecutor Shen led officials to examine the body and confirmed that he had died from poisoning. He ordered the younger brother to prepare a coffin for burial.

Zhenjiang

Jiangsu Provincial Third Plenary Session to Open 113

The third Jiangsu Provincial Congress of Representatives is scheduled to open on the 25th of this month. Representatives from various counties and provinces must arrive in the provincial capital tomorrow (the 13th) to register. The conference will last for one week. Due to the re-election of provincial executive and supervisory committee members, activities and competition among all parties are intense. Ye Xiufeng, Ni Bi, and Zheng Yitong, the three members of the preparatory committee for the Third Plenary Session specially dispatched by the Central Government to the province, have been holding meetings for days. In addition to verifying the list of provincial representatives from various counties, they decided yesterday that Gu Ziyang and Zhou Shaocheng, members of the Provincial Executive Committee, will serve on the Presidium of the Provincial Third Plenary Session. Zhang Gongren, Lan Weibin, and Ma Yuanfang of the Provincial Executive Committee, and Qiu Youqin and Duan Muzhen of the Provincial Supervisory Committee will form the Representative Qualification Review Committee, with Lan Weibin responsible for reporting on party affairs from the Provincial Executive Committee, Niu Changyao responsible for reporting on committee affairs from the Provincial Supervisory Committee, Zhou Houjun as the secretary of the General Assembly Secretariat, and Zhang Gongren as the director of the General Assembly Reception. The reception area is located within the Provincial Party Headquarters. A total of 175 representatives will attend this conference. The office has selected the Da Hua Hotel for representatives from Xuzhou and Haizhou counties, the Zhenjiang Hotel for representatives from Songjiang and Shanghai, the Wuzhou Hotel for representatives from Huai'an and Yangzhou counties, the Wanquanlou Hotel for representatives from Suzhou, Changzhou, and Zhenjiang counties, and the New Hotel for representatives from Ningguo counties.

Nantong

Tax Police Stop Car, Open Fire, and Kill a Person 114

Gu Yinglong, the principal of the Baipu District Public Elementary School, came to the city on the 20th to collect over 300 silver dollars in school funds from the Education Bureau. That evening, he boarded the Tongru Line No. 182 bus at the West Park Bus Station to return to Baipu. There were a total of eight people in the car, including the driver. When the car reached the Shibali River Estuary, Sun Ruhe, the squad leader of the Second Squad of the Twenty-Third Team of the Tax Police, and police officer Xu Jiaming stopped the car, intending to hitch a ride. The driver told them that the car was full. The tax police intended to open fire. The first bullet hit the tire, the second bullet pierced the car's roof, and the third bullet hit Gu Yinglong in the back of the head, killing him instantly. The tax police still drove the other passengers off with weapons, claiming to have killed salt smugglers and taking them to their department for investigation, forcing the driver to drive away. The crowd was indignant and immediately telegraphed the Baipu Station to intercept the police. The two officers were handed over to the county government. During the interrogation on the 21st, Sun Ruhe confessed to the shooting and killing, and was put in shackles and detained pending submission to the provincial government for review. The entire education community in the county was outraged by Gu Yinglong's tragic and untimely death, and the director of the Education Bureau, Guan Jincheng, went to the county government to request severe punishment for the murderers. The local automobile industry was also outraged by the tax police's brutality and lawlessness and went on strike. After County Magistrate Zhang's persuasion, they resumed operations on the afternoon of the 21st.

Solution to the Yuankang Coal Case 115

The Yuankang Coal Company was found to be transporting Fuzhou coal, which was discovered by the National Salvation Association. On the 20th, the Provincial Committee convened representatives from various agencies to discuss the matter and decided to fine the company 2,300 silver dollars, which the Chamber of Commerce would be responsible for paying to support the Northeast Volunteer Army.

Yangzhou

Students of Private Yangzhong School on Strike 116

All the students of the private Yangzhong school went on strike on the morning of the 21st due to economic issues and a dispute with the school. They formed a school protection committee and elected Huang Weiqing as a standing committee member. After a general meeting, they decided to strike and distribute declarations, requesting the board of directors to appoint another principal. Over 400 students marched to the homes of the school board members to petition, demanding the maintenance of the school. They first went to the home of school board member Wang Boling, but Wang was in Beijing, so they sent representatives to the home of Hu Xianbo, asking him to maintain the school and stating the reasons for the strike. Hu comforted them and asked them to relay to everyone to attend class while the school board deliberates on a solution. The representatives were satisfied and dispersed.

Guest Talk: Feng Zhanhai's Troops 119

Arduous and Extraordinary, Loyal and Brave

Tragic Circumstances Bring Tears to One's Eyes

A gentleman from Beiping sent people out of the pass to comfort Feng Zhanhai's troops. Now, a telegram from the front reports that the soldiers of Feng Zhanhai's troops have been fighting bitterly with the enemy for years, traversing thousands of miles. When ammunition ran out and reinforcements were exhausted, they had no choice but to lead their troops west, hoping to replenish them in order to return east. On the day of crossing the river, the soldiers, unable to bring their families who had not been able to escape back inside the pass beforehand, and afraid that they would be humiliated by the enemy if abandoned, mostly used their hands to cut the throats of their beloved wives and children, and set out westward in tears. Passing through the wilderness of western Liaoning, at a time when nine out of ten houses were empty, they marched non-stop, unable to eat their fill for days. The northern border was cold early, and winter clothes had not arrived. They exchanged clothes for work. The troops were not tempted by profit and not afraid of powerful enemies. They faced death many times and experienced hardships unheard of in life. What were they doing? It was only because their ambition to save the country was not fulfilled and their patriotic heart was not dead. Looking back at the country, armed comrades who are not burdened with combat missions receive salaries every month and eat their fill every day. Feng's troops' situation is vastly different. The comfort funds received at home and abroad are like a drop in the bucket, less than two-tenths of each soldier's monthly salary. The dead cannot be mourned, and the wounded cannot be rescued, but Feng's troops are still disciplined, grateful, and without complaint. Every time they think of the enemy, they are filled with anger and determined to destroy them. Feng's army is worthy of the people of the country, but the people of the country are ashamed of Feng's army. These circumstances are all clear. There is no need to elaborate further. However, as the end of the year approaches, considering human nature, the wise men at home and abroad should jointly devise a complete and effective plan to comfort their past efforts and encourage their original aspirations. Recovering the territory truly depends on them. Feng's army's loyalty and righteousness are known to the world. Such tragic circumstances have not been widely understood before. When the people of the country hear this, how can they comfort these loyal and brave soldiers who have sacrificed for the country?
